/* ============================================================
   PROOF SCENE — PHOTO DEPTH (2026-06-29): soft bottom-edge MASK so the
   portrait melts into the dark bg (no hard cut-off) + faint gold rim
   behind via .proof-scene__pic::before.
   MASK ONLY here — does NOT touch .proof-scene__photo filter, the halo
   size/opacity, or the card a/b/c positions (all user-dialed).
   Intersects a vertical bottom-fade with a soft vignette so the lower
   edge and lower corners feather away into #020305. Last-wins.
   ============================================================ */
#proof-numbers .proof-scene__photo{

    linear-gradient(to bottom,
      #000 0%, #000 58%, rgba(0,0,0,.9) 77%, rgba(0,0,0,.4) 90%, rgba(0,0,0,0) 100%),
    radial-gradient(120% 134% at 50% 30%,
      #000 56%, rgba(0,0,0,.82) 78%, rgba(0,0,0,0) 100%) !important;

    linear-gradient(to bottom,
      #000 0%, #000 58%, rgba(0,0,0,.9) 77%, rgba(0,0,0,.4) 90%, rgba(0,0,0,0) 100%),

  mask-position: center, center !important;
  -webkit-mask-composite: source-in !important; /* WebKit/Safari keyword */
  mask-composite: intersect !important;          /* standard keyword */
}
/* faint gold rim BEHIND the photo. .proof-scene__pic already has
   isolation:isolate (floor-shadow block above); ::after = floor shadow (z 0),

  /* feather the rim's own bottom so it never shows a hard edge on the bg */
  -webkit-mask-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #000 0%, #000 62%, rgba(0,0,0,0) 100%);
  mask-image: linear-gradient(to bottom, #000 0%, #000 62%, rgba(0,0,0,0) 100%);

/* ============================================================
   PROOF METRIC — CARD SHINE-SWEEP (appended; scoped; reduced-motion safe)
   Periodic premium light sweep across .proof-metric. Pure ::after overlay,
   clipped to the rounded card. Does NOT touch backdrop-filter / border /
   box-shadow / dialed positions / float animation. GPU-only transform+opacity.
   ============================================================ */

     box-shadow are unaffected (they paint on the element box, not clipped). */
  #proof-numbers .proof-metric{ overflow: hidden; }

  #proof-numbers .proof-metric .proof-metric-lbl{ position: relative; z-index: 1; }

  /* the sweep itself — a soft diagonal champagne band that glides across */

    content: "";

    z-index: 0;
    top: -40%;
    bottom: -40%;
    left: -60%;
    width: 55%;

    background: linear-gradient(
      105deg,
      rgba(245,226,184,0) 0%,
      rgba(245,226,184,0.06) 38%,
      rgba(245,200,110,0.16) 50%,
      rgba(245,226,184,0.06) 62%,
      rgba(245,226,184,0) 100%
    );
    filter: blur(2px);
    opacity: 0;
    transform: translate3d(0,0,0) rotate(8deg);
    will-change: transform, opacity;
    animation: proofMetricShine 6.2s var(--ease-out, cubic-bezier(.22,1,.36,1)) infinite;
  }

  /* staggered start per card so they shimmer out of phase */
  #proof-numbers .proof-metric--a::after{ animation-delay: 0s; }
  #proof-numbers .proof-metric--b::after{ animation-delay: -2s; animation-duration: 6.8s; }
  #proof-numbers .proof-metric--c::after{ animation-delay: -4s; animation-duration: 7.2s; }

  /* travel: enter from left, glide fully across, fade at the edges.
     translateX in % is relative to the ::after's own width (55% of card),
     so ~360% carries it from off-left to off-right of the card. */
  @keyframes proofMetricShine{
    0%   { transform: translate3d(0,0,0) rotate(8deg);     opacity: 0; }
    8%   { opacity: 1; }
    50%  { opacity: 1; }
    62%  { transform: translate3d(360%,0,0) rotate(8deg);  opacity: 0; }
    100% { transform: translate3d(360%,0,0) rotate(8deg);  opacity: 0; }
  }

  /* MOBILE: cards stack statically — suppress the sweep to keep it calm */
  @media (max-width: 860px){
    #proof-numbers .proof-metric::after{ animation: none; opacity: 0; }
  }
}

    animation: none !important;

/* ============================================================
   PROOF SCENE — SCROLL-SNAP REMOVED (2026-06-29)
   The proximity snap + scroll-snap-stop:always felt "stuck" / not smooth
   (the user: "remove that stuck effect the scroll is not smooth"). A snap
   that forces a rest WILL fight the wheel. Removed entirely — native scroll
   is buttery. The "don't miss the proof" goal is now handled by the
   scroll-driven PROOF ENTRANCE below (a smooth rise-into-view, no snap). */
@media (prefers-reduced-motion: no-preference){
  /* (scroll-snap intentionally NOT set here — see PROOF ENTRANCE block) */
}

/* ============================================================
   PROOF ENTRANCE — "PRESENTS ITSELF" (2026-06-29)
   The proof already slides UP over the sticky hero (the .content-panel /
   .hero--editorial "Madquick" cover). This makes that slide DELIBERATE so
   visitors can't miss the proof or the person:
     • Pure CSS `animation-timeline: view()` — NO scroll-snap, NO forced rest,
       NO JS, NO clip. Compositor-scrubbed against each element's own viewport
       pass, so it tracks wheel velocity instead of capturing it (no "atke").
     • Drives ONLY inner children of the proof scene — NEVER #proof-numbers or
       .content-panel (a transform there makes a containing block and kills the
       sticky-hero pin that IS the modal cover).
     • The PERSON resolves FIRST (biggest lift + a whisper of scale), his proof
       cards ride in on the sheet, the copy lands LAST -> "presenting itself".
     • Photo chain stays overflow:visible -> the cut-out glow is never boxed.
     • Every range completes EARLY (by entry 100%, before the `cover` phase) so
       the forced inner min-height can't truncate the reveal on tall viewports.
   Three safety nets below guarantee the proof is NEVER blank (unsupported
   browser / reduced-motion / timeline edge-case).
   ============================================================ */
@supports (animation-timeline: view()) {
  @media (prefers-reduced-motion: no-preference) {

    /* (graft: modal LIP) soft lit top edge on the rising sheet. NO transform
       on the panel (would break the sticky hero); a ::before hairline-gold glow
       masked to transparent, hugging the existing rounded top corners — fades
       in as the panel lifts off the hero. No box, respects the transparent bg. */
    .content-panel::before{
      content: "";
      position: absolute; left: 0; right: 0; top: -1px;
      height: clamp(54px, 8vh, 120px);
      pointer-events: none; z-index: 2;
      border-radius: inherit;
      background: linear-gradient(180deg,
        rgba(216,167,62,0.20) 0%,
        rgba(216,167,62,0.06) 28%,
        transparent 80%);
      -webkit-mask-image: linear-gradient(180deg, #000 0%, transparent 100%);
              mask-image: linear-gradient(180deg, #000 0%, transparent 100%);
      opacity: 0;
      animation: pe-lip linear both;
      animation-timeline: view();
      animation-range: entry 6% entry 60%;
    }
    @keyframes pe-lip{ from{ opacity: 0; } to{ opacity: 1; } }

    /* (graft: unified sheet) the whole grid rises as one modal sheet. Safe to
       transform/opacity here — .proof-scene__inner carries NO .reveal and is not
       in the force-show wall. HIGH opacity floor (0.86) so the group composite
       never hides the force-shown headline/cards/chart behind their own
       !important; the per-element keyframes do the materialize. */
    #proof-numbers.proof-scene .proof-scene__inner{
      transform-origin: 50% 100%;
      animation: pe-sheet linear both;
      animation-timeline: view();
      animation-range: entry 2% entry 90%;
    }
    @keyframes pe-sheet{
      from{ opacity: 0.86; transform: translateY(26px) scale(0.985); }
      to  { opacity: 1;    transform: none; }
    }

    /* THE PERSON, presented FIRST. id+class+!important OUT-specifies the
       force-show wall (.proof-scene__visual.reveal{opacity:1!important}), so the
       native keyframe owns the entrance. Biggest travel + a whisper of scale so
       the cut-out steps toward the viewer like a modal opening. overflow stays
       visible -> radial glow never boxes. */
    #proof-numbers.proof-scene .proof-scene__visual.reveal{
      /* NO !important on opacity/transform — important author beats CSS
         animations, which would freeze the photo. The animation OWNS them.
         (The force-show wall no longer pins this element, see ~line 9307.)
         Shorthand-then-timeline/range = same working pattern as the inner. */
      transform-origin: 50% 70%;
      animation: pe-present linear both;
      animation-timeline: view();
      animation-range: entry 0% entry 64%;
    }
    @keyframes pe-present{
      from{ opacity: 0; transform: translateY(34px) scale(0.965); }
      60% { opacity: 1; }
      to  { opacity: 1; transform: none; }
    }

    /* THE RIGHT COPY, lands LAST so the eye finishes on the person then reads
       "Your growth is my job." .pscene-copy has NO .reveal and isn't in the
       force-show wall -> no !important war. */
    #proof-numbers.proof-scene .pscene-copy{
      opacity: 0;
      animation: pe-present-soft linear both;
      animation-timeline: view();
      animation-range: entry 10% entry 86%;
      transform-origin: 0% 50%;
    }
    @keyframes pe-present-soft{
      from{ opacity: 0; transform: translateY(20px); }
      to  { opacity: 1; transform: none; }
    }

    /* NOTE: the three floating .proof-metric cards are deliberately NOT animated
       here — they run the perpetual proofMetricFloat transform and are pinned
       opacity:1. Overriding their `animation` shorthand would KILL the float.
       They ride in on the parent .proof-scene__inner sheet lift instead. */
  }
}

/* SAFETY NET A: if animation-timeline is unsupported the @supports block is
   ignored entirely and the proof renders via the existing .reveal IO path +
   force-show wall. Explicitly pin the two elements NOT in that wall so a
   timeline edge-case can't leave them at opacity:0. */
@supports not (animation-timeline: view()){
  #proof-numbers.proof-scene .proof-scene__inner,
  #proof-numbers.proof-scene .proof-scene__visual.reveal,
  #proof-numbers.proof-scene .pscene-copy{ opacity: 1; transform: none; }
}

/* SAFETY NET B: reduced-motion freezes everything fully arrived (last + media
   query so it out-specifies the @supports block). */
@media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce){
  .content-panel::before{ display: none !important; }
  #proof-numbers.proof-scene .proof-scene__inner,
  #proof-numbers.proof-scene .proof-scene__visual.reveal,
  #proof-numbers.proof-scene .pscene-copy{
    opacity: 1 !important;
    transform: none !important;
    animation: none !important;
  }
}

/* ============================================================
   HERO CARD — SHINE-SWEEP ("chok chok") (2026-06-29)
   THE effect the user means: a soft champagne light band that GLIDES
   left->right across each card (specular shine sweep) — like the proof
   cards. Pure ::after overlay, clipped to the rounded card, GPU
   transform+opacity, staggered out of phase. Mirrors proofMetricShine.
   ============================================================ */
@media (prefers-reduced-motion: no-preference){

/* ===== DRAW-IN MECHANICS (GPU: transform/opacity/stroke-dashoffset) =========
   Default (final) state below = everything resolved, so no-JS/no-IO/reduced-
   motion render the finished graphic instantly with NO flash. JS ARMS a card
   by adding .skl-armed (sets start state) then .skl-play (animates to final),
   re-arming on each enter. Without JS, .skl-armed never appears -> final. */

/* LINE / AREA: pen-draw left->right. JS sets --len = path length. */
.skl-card [data-skl-line]{ stroke-dasharray:var(--len,600); }
.skl-card.skl-armed [data-skl-line]{
  stroke-dasharray:var(--len,600); stroke-dashoffset:var(--len,600);
}
.skl-card.skl-play [data-skl-line]{
  stroke-dashoffset:0;
  transition:stroke-dashoffset 1.15s var(--ease-out) .12s;
}
.skl-card.skl-armed [data-skl-area]{ opacity:0; transform:translateY(8px); }
.skl-card.skl-play  [data-skl-area]{
  opacity:.95; transform:none;
  transition:opacity .9s var(--ease-out), transform .9s var(--ease-out);
}
.skl-card.skl-armed [data-skl-dot]{ opacity:0; transform:scale(0); transform-box:fill-box; transform-origin:center; }
.skl-card.skl-play  [data-skl-dot]{
  opacity:1; transform:scale(1);
  transition:opacity .3s ease 1.05s, transform .42s var(--ease-spring) 1.05s;
}

/* BARS: grow scaleY 0->1 from the bottom, staggered by --i */
.skl-bar,.skl-row,.skl-clip,.skl-shape,.skl-gnode,.skl-loop__node{ transform-box:fill-box; }
.skl-card.skl-armed .skl-bar{ transform:scaleY(0); transform-origin:bottom; }
.skl-card.skl-play  .skl-bar{
  transform:scaleY(1); transform-origin:bottom;
  transition:transform .55s var(--ease-out);
  transition-delay:calc(var(--i,0) * 90ms);
}

/* ARCS (content marketing): each arc sweeps via dashoffset, staggered */
.skl-card [data-skl-arc]{ stroke-dasharray:var(--len,400); }
.skl-card.skl-armed [data-skl-arc]{ stroke-dasharray:var(--len,400); stroke-dashoffset:var(--len,400); }
.skl-card.skl-play  [data-skl-arc]{

    <p class="eyebrow">Plain-language policy</p>
    <h1>Privacy &amp; portfolio evidence.</h1>
    <p class="lead">This page explains what information the portfolio handles, how contact links work, and how project evidence is selected for public display.</p>

    <div class="policy">
      <h2>Contact information</h2>
      <p>This website does not currently use a contact form. If you contact me through email, WhatsApp or LinkedIn, the information you send is handled by that service and used only to respond to your message, discuss relevant work, or continue a professional conversation.</p>

      <h2>Analytics and cookies</h2>
      <p>The portfolio does not currently install behavioral analytics, advertising pixels or session-replay tools. If measurement is added later, this policy will be updated before those tools go live, and the implementation will avoid sending message content or unnecessary personal information.</p>

      <h2>Portfolio evidence</h2>
      <p>Results shown here come from owned properties or permission-safe summaries of professional work. Major claims should state the relevant source, period and my role. Client-sensitive information, private URLs and personal identifiers are removed or redacted before public publication.</p>

      <h2>External services</h2>
      <p>The site links to third-party services such as WhatsApp, LinkedIn, Instagram and client websites. Their privacy practices apply after you follow those links.</p>

      <h2>Questions or correction requests</h2>
      <p>To ask what information I hold from a direct enquiry, request a correction, or report portfolio material that should be reviewed, email <a href="mailto:growabhijit@gmail.com"><strong>growabhijit@gmail.com</strong></a>.</p>
    </div>
    <p class="updated">Last reviewed: 30 June 2026</p>
